};

                 <h3 class="OptionPreviewList-SectionTitle" itemprop="text"><a class="_section-link _section-title-link" href="/topics/1374/viewpoints/3/~frameworks-for-developing-cross-platform-mobile-apps-with-javascript~react-native#1" rel="nofollow">

                   </div> Allows you to develop native apps</a></h3>

                  React Native allows you to create native apps by generating native views with JavaScript instead of using a web wrapper.

                 <h3 class="OptionPreviewList-SectionTitle" itemprop="text"><a class="_section-link _section-title-link" href="/topics/1374/viewpoints/3/~frameworks-for-developing-cross-platform-mobile-apps-with-javascript~react-native#2" rel="nofollow">
                   <div class="_is-con OptionPreviewList-SectionTitle-Type con">
                    Con
                   </div> Steep learning curve</a></h3>
                 <div class="OptionPreviewList-SectionText _has-text _section-description-link" itemprop="text">
                  React Native is not the most beginner-friendly framework for creating mobile apps with JavaScript. It requires that the developer know React, which is known to have a steep learning curve.
                 </div>
                </div>

                 <h3 class="OptionPreviewList-SectionTitle" itemprop="text"><a class="_section-link _section-title-link" href="/topics/1374/viewpoints/3/~frameworks-for-developing-cross-platform-mobile-apps-with-javascript~react-native#5" rel="nofollow">
                   <div class="_is-con OptionPreviewList-SectionTitle-Type con">
                    Con
                   </div> If core team doesn't use a certain feature, it's not developed</a></h3>
                 <div class="OptionPreviewList-SectionText _has-text _section-description-link" itemprop="text">
                  Whenever there's functionality you need that they don't use in their apps, it's not going to get developed by them, even if it's obvious it should be in the core. They always say to either submit a PR or create a separate module.
                 </div>
                </div>

                   <div class="_is-con OptionPreviewList-SectionTitle-Type con">
                    Con
                   </div> Nativescript + Angular apps for Android tend to have long startup times.</a></h3>
                 <div class="OptionPreviewList-SectionText _has-text _section-description-link" itemprop="text">
                  It's very difficult to have acceptable startup times with NS+Angular in Android. It's not uncommon to see apps taking 6 sec or more to start AFTER having been optimized with Webpack (mandatory!). The same app in iOS takes only 2-3 sec. Also, this seems to happen only with the NS+Angular fla...

               <a class="_option-link _option-title-link OptionPreviewList-OptionTitle" href="/topics/1374/viewpoints/13/~frameworks-for-developing-cross-platform-mobile-apps-with-javascript~polymer" title="Polymer" rel="nofollow"><h2 class="OptionPreviewList-OptionTitle-Text"><span itemprop="name">Polymer</span></h2></a>

               <div class="OptionPreviewList-Section">
                <div class="OptionPreviewList-SectionContent">
                 <h3 class="OptionPreviewList-SectionTitle" itemprop="text"><a class="_section-link _section-title-link" href="/topics/1374/viewpoints/13/~frameworks-for-developing-cross-platform-mobile-apps-with-javascript~polymer#1" rel="nofollow">
                   <div class="_is-pro OptionPreviewList-SectionTitle-Type pro">
                    Pro
                   </div> Based on W3C's web components</a></h3>
                 <div class="OptionPreviewList-SectionText _has-text _section-description-link" itemprop="text">
                  Web Components are a collection of specifications released by W3C as a way to reduce the complexity of web apps by creating reusable components. Browser support is currently poor for web components, however Polymer is developed to make web components compatible with modern browsers.
                 </div>
                </div>
                <div class="_has-link-bar OptionPreviewList-SectionLinks LinkBar">
                 <a class="_section-reaction-dropdown-link LinkBar-More"></a>
                 <div class="OptionPreviewList-Section-ReactionButtons">
                  <div class="_ReactionButtonAgreeView ReactionButtonSet-Item OptionPreviewList-Section-ReactionButton" data-local-id="kwW5wdjH1495" data-view="ReactionButtonAgreeView">
                   <a class="_reaction-toggle-link ReactionButtonSet-Link"><button class="_reaction-tooltip-link ReactionButton _reacted-class"><img class="ReactionButton-Icon" src="/images/icons/detailed/tick.svg"> 1</button></a>
                  </div>
                  <div class="_ReactionButtonDisagreeView ReactionButtonSet-Item OptionPreviewList-Section-ReactionButton" data-local-id="kwW5wdjH1495" data-view="ReactionButtonDisagreeView">

                  </div>

                </div>
               </div>

               <div class="OptionPreviewList-Section">
                <div class="OptionPreviewList-SectionContent">
                 <h3 class="OptionPreviewList-SectionTitle" itemprop="text"><a class="_section-link _section-title-link" href="/topics/1374/viewpoints/13/~frameworks-for-developing-cross-platform-mobile-apps-with-javascript~polymer#2" rel="nofollow">
                   <div class="_is-pro OptionPreviewList-SectionTitle-Type pro">
                    Pro
                   </div> Component based</a></h3>
                 <div class="OptionPreviewList-SectionText _has-text _section-description-link" itemprop="text">
                  Polymer apps are component based. You have to break down the layout of your UI into components, which makes it easier to understand how every part of the application works and how they relate with each other. This way it's also easier to maintain the application.
                 </div>
                </div>

              <div class="_SummaryPageSectionView OptionPreviewList-SectionWrapper _list" data-local-id="kwW5wdjH1521" data-view="SummaryPageSectionView">
               <div class="_MultiUserView ComboAvatar" data-local-id="kwW5wdjH1526" data-view="MultiUserView">
                <div class="_section-users-tooltip-link ComboAvatar-TooltipLink">
                 <div class="_has-one-user _most-recent-user ComboAvatar-Image main Avatar singleImage" data-initials="a" data-background="2">
                  <img class="_most-recent-user-image" src="https://graph.facebook.com/100004752396899/picture?width=50&amp;height=50" alt="Andris Pelcbergs">
                 </div>
                </div>
               </div>
               <div class="OptionPreviewList-Section">
                <div class="OptionPreviewList-SectionContent">
                 <h3 class="OptionPreviewList-SectionTitle" itemprop="text"><a class="_section-link _section-title-link" href="/topics/1374/viewpoints/13/~frameworks-for-developing-cross-platform-mobile-apps-with-javascript~polymer#3" rel="nofollow">
                   <div class="_is-con OptionPreviewList-SectionTitle-Type con">
                    Con
                   </div> No server side rendering</a></h3>
                 <div class="OptionPreviewList-SectionText _has-text _section-description-link" itemprop="text">
                  Polymer does not support server-side rendering. This results in higher loading times, more HTTP requests and it's not very SEO friendly, since search engines have no way of indexing a page if it's not rendered in the server.
                 </div>
                </div>
                <div class="_has-link-bar OptionPreviewList-SectionLinks LinkBar">
                 <a class="_section-reaction-dropdown-link LinkBar-More"></a>
                 <div class="OptionPreviewList-Section-ReactionButtons">
                  <div class="_ReactionButtonAgreeView ReactionButtonSet-Item OptionPreviewList-Section-ReactionButton" data-local-id="kwW5wdjH1524" data-view="ReactionButtonAgreeView">

                  </div>
                  <div class="_ReactionButtonDisagreeView ReactionButtonSet-Item OptionPreviewList-Section-ReactionButton" data-local-id="kwW5wdjH1524" data-view="ReactionButtonDisagreeView">
                   <a class="_reaction-toggle-link ReactionButtonSet-Link"><button class="_reaction-tooltip-link ReactionButton _reacted-class"><img class="ReactionButton-Icon" src="/images/icons/detailed/cross.svg"> 1</button></a>

                <div class="OptionPreviewList-SectionContent">
                 <h3 class="OptionPreviewList-SectionTitle" itemprop="text"><a class="_section-link _section-title-link" href="/topics/1374/viewpoints/13/~frameworks-for-developing-cross-platform-mobile-apps-with-javascript~polymer#5" rel="nofollow">
                   <div class="_is-con OptionPreviewList-SectionTitle-Type con">
                    Con
                   </div> Slow performance in mobile</a></h3>
                 <div class="OptionPreviewList-SectionText _has-text _section-description-link" itemprop="text">
                  Since most mobile web browsers don't have a very powerful JS engine, Polymer can be a little slow for mobile devices.
                 </div>

                 <h3 class="OptionPreviewList-SectionTitle" itemprop="text"><a class="_section-link _section-title-link" href="/topics/1374/viewpoints/19/~frameworks-for-developing-cross-platform-mobile-apps-with-javascript~fuse#1" rel="nofollow">

                 <h3 class="OptionPreviewList-SectionTitle" itemprop="text"><a class="_section-link _section-title-link" href="/topics/1374/viewpoints/19/~frameworks-for-developing-cross-platform-mobile-apps-with-javascript~fuse#4" rel="nofollow">
                   <div class="_is-pro OptionPreviewList-SectionTitle-Type pro">
                    Pro
                   </div> OpenGL UI</a></h3>
                 <div class="OptionPreviewList-SectionText _has-text _section-description-link" itemprop="text">
